<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper presents an inductorless low-noise amplifier (LNA) design for an ultra-wideband (UWB) receiver front-end. A current-reuse gain-enhanced noise canceling architecture is proposed, and the properties and limitations of the gain-enhancement stage are discussed. Capacitive peaking is employed to improve the gain flatness and -3-dB bandwidth, at the cost of absolute gain value. The LNA circuit is fabricated in a 0.13-mum triple-well CMOS technology. Measurement result shows that a small-signal gain of 11 dB and a -3-dB bandwidth of 2-9.6 GHz are obtained. Over the -3-dB bandwidth, the input return loss is less than -8.3 dB, and the noise figure is 3.6-4.8 dB. The LNA consumes 19 mW from a low supply voltage of 1.5 V. It is shown that the LNA designed without on-chip inductors achieves comparable performances with inductor-based designs. The silicon area is reduced significantly in the inductorless design, the LNA core occupies only 0.05 mm<sup>2</sup>, which is among the smallest reported designs.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Wideband and ultra-wideband (UWB) low-noise amplifiers (LNAs) have received extensive research interest over recent years. A wide range of modern and future communication systems has been proposed that operates over a bandwidth exceeding several gigahertz, e.g., software-defined radio, UWB, etc. UWB systems are regulated within the spectrum of 3.1–10.6 GHz and are capable of data rate up to gigabits per second <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. This poses a more stringent requirement on the UWB transceiver <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a> especially for the front-end LNA, which has to provide an ultra-wide bandwidth with reasonable noise figure (NF) and impedance matching. Minimizing supply voltage and power consumption is always demanded for portable applications.</p><p>Traditionally, these types of wideband amplifiers were implemented with balanced or distributed architectures that were originally used in microwave circuit design <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. However, the large area occupation and high power dissipation of the traveling-wave amplifier make it infeasible for low-power single-chip integration. Recently, a distributed amplifier has been reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, which achieves comparable performance with lumped design in terms of power and area consumption.</p><p>With the development of advanced semiconductor technology, lumped implementation of the LNA in CMOS and SiGe BiCMOS has been pushed up to tens of gigahertz <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>. There are also a few UWB LNAs that have been reported in the literature. Various circuit techniques have been proposed to enhance the bandwidth.</p><p>A classical approach to widening bandwidth is negative feedback, which is normally realized in the form of resistive shunt feedback <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a>. The feedback can also be implemented using an active circuit <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a> or a transformer <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a>. Meanwhile, standalone negative feedback can hardly achieve sufficient bandwidth; the inductor peaking technique is often adopted in these feedback-based designs. Further, the analysis presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a> shows that resistive feedback amplifiers cannot provide required performance with low power consumption. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_1">[21]</a>, UWB LNAs with multisection impedance matching are reported, which expand the use of an inductor-degenerated amplifier with emphasis on wideband impedance matching. This approach is efficient in terms of bandwidth and has been proven in both CMOS and SiGe BiCMOS technologies. However, the extra passive devices used for matching purpose increase design complexity and area occupation. Recently, a combined feedback architecture for UWB LNA design has been reported <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_1">[22]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_1">[23]</a>. Adopted from microwave circuits <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_1">[24]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_1">[25]</a>, the resistive feedback is applied both globally and locally. This architecture achieves sufficient bandwidth and gain even without inductors. However, potential instability problem occurs due to multiple feedback loops. High transconductance device is also required for bandwidth–gain tradeoff. Thus, this configuration has not been realized in standard CMOS technology.</p><p>Compared with narrowband LNA designs, a severe tradeoff between NF and source impedance matching exists in a wideband LNA. Most of the reported UWB LNA designs are focused on bandwidth enhancement. As a result, a few of them achieve comparable noise performance with narrowband LNAs. A CMOS UWB LNA employing the noise-canceling technique is reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_1">[26]</a>, where thermal noise of the input matching device can be sensed and canceled by the feed-forward configuration <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_1">[27]</a>. This avoids potential instability due to global negative feedback. However, the gain performance of such a configuration is often less superior.</p><p>This paper presents a UWB LNA with comprehensive considerations on NF and wideband gain performance. A modified noise sensing and canceling architecture is exploited, which employs a current-reuse stage for gain compensation. Inductorless design is also explored. Bandwidth enhancement is achieved by capacitive peaking.</p><p><a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> reviews wideband noise canceling techniques. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> presents a modified wideband noise canceling architecture capable of higher gain performance, and the properties and considerations are discussed in detail. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>, approaches to bandwidth enhancement are discussed and an inductorless approach using capacitive peaking is presented. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a> shows the experimental results of the demonstrated LNA circuit. This paper is finally concluded in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec6" class="fulltext-link">Section VI</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Review of Wideband Noise Canceling</h2></div><p>The wideband LNA design exploiting thermal noise canceling was originally presented by Bruccoleri et al. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_2">[27]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_2">[28]</a>. The idea is briefly introduced as follows. Consider the LNA circuit shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>, the wideband input impedance matching is realized by a common-source stage with resistive shunt feedback. The noise current of <i>M</i>1 (and <i>M</i>2) flows out of the node <i>B</i> through feedback resistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{f}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-9" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">R_{f}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and source impedance to the ground, leading to two equal-signed noise voltages at nodes <i>A</i> and <i>B</i>. They are subsequently amplified by a combining stage, where opposite-signed noise voltages are produced by the source–follower (see from <i>B</i>) and common-source amplifier (see from <i>A</i>). By carefully designing the circuit parameters, the noise contribution of matching device <i>M</i>1 (and <i>M</i>2) can be canceled. width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-61"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-62"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-63" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">R_{s}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the source impedance. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{v,2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-64" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-65"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-66"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-67" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-68"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-69"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-70" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">v</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-71" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-72" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">A_{v,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> denotes the gain of the output common-source stage (<i>M</i>3 to <i>M</i>4). This equation is determined by the noise sampling mechanism of the input stage. Note that <i>M</i>2 is not necessarily needed by the noise canceling principle, it increases the effective <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">g_{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-73" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-74"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-75"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-76" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-77"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-78"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-79" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">g_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the input matching stage where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm IN} \approx 1/{g_{mi}} = 1/(g_{m1}+g_{m2})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-80" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-81"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-82"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-83" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-84"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-85"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-86" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">I</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-87" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">N</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-88" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≈</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-89" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-90"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-91"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-92" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-93"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-94"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-95"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-96" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-97"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-98"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-99" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-100" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-101" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-102" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-103"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-104"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-105" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-106" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-107"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-108" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-109"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-110"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-111" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-112" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-113" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-114" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-115" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-116"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-117"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-119" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-120" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">Z_{\rm IN} \approx 1/{g_{mi}} = 1/(g_{m1}+g_{m2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. On the other hand, the signal voltages at nodes <i>A</i> and <i>B</i> have an opposite sign as long as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">g_{mi}R_{f}&gt;1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-121" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-122"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-123"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-124" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-125"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-127" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-129"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-130" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-132"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-133" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-134" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&gt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-135" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">g_{mi}R_{f}&gt;1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>; thus, the combining stage produces equal-signed output signal voltages and adds them up. The noise contribution of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{f}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-136" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-137"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-138"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-139" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-140"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">R_{f}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the combining stage cannot be canceled in this configuration, they dominate the noise performance of the overall LNA. An inductorless LNA is demonstrated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_2">[27]</a>, which achieves 13.7-dB voltage gain, 0.002–1.6-GHz <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-{\hbox {3-dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-143" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-144"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-145" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-146"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-147"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-148"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-149"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-150" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3-dB</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">-{\hbox {3-dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> bandwidth, and less than 2.4-dB NF in 0.25-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {m}} </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-151" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-152"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-153" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-154"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-155"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-156"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-157"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-158" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">\mu{\hbox {m}} </script></tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4339599/4339618/4339618-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4339599/4339618/4339618-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Simplified wideband LNA architectures exploiting thermal noise canceling.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4339618/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>An alternative noise canceling configuration, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>, is also proposed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_2">[27]</a>, and has been successfully implemented for UWB in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_2">[26]</a>. In this configuration, a common-gate stage (<i>M</i>1) is employed for wideband input matching. Designed in 0.18-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {m}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-159" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-160"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-161" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-163"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-164"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-165"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-166" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS, 9.7-dB gain, 1.2–11.9-GHz <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-{\hbox {3-dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-167" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-168"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-169" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-170"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-171"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-172"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-173"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-174" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3-dB</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">-{\hbox {3-dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> bandwidth, and 4.5–5.1-dB NF (over 3.1–10.6 GHz) are obtained in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_2">[26]</a>.</p><p>Review of the above results shows that there is less freedom in controlling the gain performance in noise canceling architectures, especially in the gigahertz range. For the matching stage using resistive shunt feedback [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>], although the noise restraints are relaxed, the input matching requirement limits the voltage gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{v}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-175" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-176"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-177"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-178" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-179"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-180"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-181" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">v</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">A_{v}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of such stages <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_2">[20]</a>. A common-gate input stage [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>] cannot provide high gain as well. For the output combining stage, the gain is constrained by the noise canceling principle, where the value of gain in two paths should produce two equal-amplitude noise voltages so that they can be canceled <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_2">[26]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_2">[27]</a>. As a result, both designs encounter architectural difficulties in achieving higher gain. Comparing to SiGe BiCMOS where higher <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">g_{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-182" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-183"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-184"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-185" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-186"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-187"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-188" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">g_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is available, the gain issue becomes more severe when it applies to CMOS. In fact, the design in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_2">[26]</a> has incorporated an additional common-source output stage (<i>M</i>4) to enhance the gain to 9.7 dB. However, this stage contributes extra noise to the output. This cannot be canceled, resulting in well above 3-dB overall NF. In this case, there is little noise cancellation observed.</p><p>Note that the noise combining stage can also be designed using a wideband transformer <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_2">[29]</a>, where the amplification is achieved at the cost of silicon area instead of power. However, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{v,2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-189" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-190"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-191"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-192" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-193"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-194"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-195" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">v</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-196" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-197" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">A_{v,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is still limited by the noise canceling condition, and the use of transformer limits the bandwidth of the LNA.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Gain-Enhanced Wideband Noise Canceling Architecture</h2></div><p>A gain-enhanced noise canceling architecture is presented here. The purpose of gain enhancement is not only on improving the gain of noise canceling architectures, but also on creating more freedom in tradeoffs involving gain. As the inductorless approach will be explored in this paper, parasitic capacitances cannot be driven with an inductor-peaking method. To achieve ultra-wide bandwidth, extensive tradeoff between bandwidth and gain may be required. Thus, a higher gain configuration offers more flexibilities for such tradeoff.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Architecture and Analysis</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> shows the modified architecture of a wideband noise-canceling LNA. A current-reused amplification stage including <i>M</i>2–<i>R</i>2, <i>M</i>3–<i>R</i>3, and <i>C</i>2 is adopted between the noise sensing and combining stages. <i>M</i>2–<i>R</i>2 and <i>M</i>3–<i>R</i>3 are stacked gain blocks within the same dc current branch. <i>C</i>2 is a large decoupling capacitor that creates a ground node at RF. This stage provides two feed-forward paths concurrently. Meanwhile, the current reuse permits higher efficiency of power and available voltage headroom <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_3a">[30]</a>. <i>R</i>8 is employed to provide extra current to the gain stack <i>M</i>2–<i>R</i>2, which will be discussed later. Note that the input parasitic capacitance degrades both input matching and noise sensing <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_3a">[20]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_3a">[27]</a>. As the target frequency of the design is up to 10 GHz, it is important to keep the input parasitics as small as possible. Thus, the input stage in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a> is replaced by a simple nMOS common-source stage. As a result, this stage would consume slightly more current for impedance matching.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4339599/4339618/4339618-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4339599/4339618/4339618-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Architecture of gain-enhanced wideband LNA with thermal noise canceling.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4339618/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Intuitively, the gain ratio of the two feed-forward paths can be kept unchanged if the parameters of <i>M</i>2–<i>R</i>2 and <i>M</i>3–<i>R</i>3 are given the same values (and without <i>R</i>8). Therefore, the noise canceling condition presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_3a">[27]</a> is retained with improved absolute gain values available. However, the gain-enhancement stage contributes additional noise as well. Using the same parameters for both <i>M</i>2–<i>R</i>2 and <i>M</i>3–<i>R</i>3 is not always the optimal choice in terms of overall noise performance. This can be analyzed as follows.</p><p>At node <i>C</i>, the noise voltage due to <i>M</i>3 and <i>R</i>3 can be expressed as <disp-formula id="deqn2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\overline {v^{2}_{n,c}}=4kT \cdot \left({\rm NEF} \cdot g_{m3} + {{ 1}\over { R_{3}}}\right)R_{3}^{2} \cdot \Delta f \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-198" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 21.745em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 17.541em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-1.619em 1017.54em 1.144em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; margin-left: -8.766em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.405em 1017.54em 5.168em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 17.541em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.405em 1017.54em 5.168em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 50%; margin-left: -8.766em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-210"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-211"><span class="munderover" id="MathJax-Span-212"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-293"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-294"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-295" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">{\rm NEF}=\gamma \cdot g_{{\rm ds}0}/g_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the noise excess factor. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">g_{{\rm ds}0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-296" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-297"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-298"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-299" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-301"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-302"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-303"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-304" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">d</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-305" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-306" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">g_{{\rm ds}0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the channel conductance when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm DS}=0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-307" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-311"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-312"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-313" style="font-size: 70.7%; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-316" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">V_{\rm DS}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For submicrometer MOSFETs, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm NEF}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-317" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-328"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-329"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-330"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-331"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-332" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">d</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-333" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-334" style="font-size: 70.7%; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-340"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-341"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-342" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-343" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&gt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-344" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">g_{{\rm ds}0}/g_{m}&gt;1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\gamma &gt;1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-345" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">\gamma &gt;1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-350" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; Note that in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a>, flicker noise is not considered due to the high-frequency operation.</p><p>Practically, we have <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm NEF} \cdot g_{m3} \gg 1/R_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-354" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-368" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≫</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-369" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; Also we consider the noise per unit bandwidth. Thus, <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> can be simplified as <disp-formula id="deqn3" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\overline {V^{2}_{n,c}}=4kT \cdot {\rm NEF} \cdot g_{m3} R_{3}^{2}.\eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-378" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block;
